#eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Sources: <a href="/wiki/Statistics_Netherlands" title="Statistics Netherlands">CBS</a><sup id="cite_ref-CBS_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBS-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Schiphol_Group" title="Schiphol Group">Schiphol Group</a><sup id="cite_ref-annualreportschiphol.com_Traffic_Review_2020_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annualreportschiphol.com_Traffic_Review_2020-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_Information_Publication" title="Aeronautical Information Publication">AIP</a><sup id="cite_ref-AIP_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Amsterdam Airport Schiphol</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>AMS</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EHAM</b>), <a href="/wiki/Pars_pro_toto" title="Pars pro toto">known informally as</a> <b>Schiphol Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Luchthaven Schiphol</i>, <small>pronounced&#32;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[\xcb\x8cl\xca\x8fxt\xc9\xa6a\xcb\x90v\xc9\x99(n) \xcb\x88sx\xc9\xaap(\xc9\xa6)\xc9\x94l]</a></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> is the main <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>. It is located 9 kilometres (5.6 miles)<sup id="cite_ref-AIP_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> southwest of <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, in the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Haarlemmermeer" title="Haarlemmermeer">Haarlemmermeer</a> in the province of <a href="/wiki/North_Holland" title="North Holland">North Holland</a>. With almost 72 million passengers in 2019, it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">third-busiest airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> in terms of passenger volume and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_by_aircraft_movements" title="List of busiest airports by aircraft movements">busiest in Europe</a> in terms of aircraft movements. With an annual cargo tonnage of 1.74 million, it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_by_cargo_traffic" title="List of busiest airports by cargo traffic">4th busiest</a> in Europe. AMS covers a total area of 6,887 acres (10.3 sq mi; 2,787 ha) of land.<sup id="cite_ref-landArea_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-landArea-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The airport is built on the single-terminal concept: one large terminal split into three large departure halls.\n</p><p>Schiphol is the hub for <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a> and its regional affiliate <a href="/wiki/KLM_Cityhopper" title="KLM Cityhopper">KLM Cityhopper</a> as well as for <a href="/wiki/Corendon_Dutch_Airlines" title="Corendon Dutch Airlines">Corendon Dutch Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martinair" title="Martinair">Martinair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transavia" title="Transavia">Transavia</a> and <a href="/wiki/TUI_fly_Netherlands" title="TUI fly Netherlands">TUI fly Netherlands</a>. The airport also serves as a base for <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a>.\n</p><p>Schiphol opened on 16 September 1916 as a military airbase. The end of the First World War also saw the beginning of civilian use of Schiphol Airport and the airport eventually lost its military role completely. By 1940, Schiphol had four asphalt runways at 45-degree angles. The airport was captured by the German military that same year and renamed <i>Fliegerhorst Schiphol</i>. The airport was destroyed through bombing but at the end of the war, the airfield was soon rebuilt. In 1949, it was decided that Schiphol was to become the primary airport of the Netherlands. Schiphol Airport was voted the Best Airport in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a> in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>According to the airport\'s media department,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> the name of Schiphol originated in the 15th century. In the language of that time, it indicated an area of low lying wetland ("hol" or "holl") where wood (scip) could be extracted.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Description">Description</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Description">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Schiphol Airport is an important European airport, ranking as Europe\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">third busiest</a> and the world\'s <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s busiest airports by passenger traffic">eleventh busiest</a> by total passenger traffic in 2017 (12th in 2016, 14th in 2015, 2014 and 2013 and 16th in 2012). It also ranks as the world\'s fifth busiest by international passenger traffic and the world\'s <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_cargo_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s busiest airports by cargo traffic">sixteenth busiest for cargo tonnage</a>. 63,625,664 passengers passed through the airport in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Schiphol\'s main competitors in terms of passenger traffic and cargo throughput are <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">London-Heathrow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Charles de Gaulle Airport">Paris\xe2\x80\x93Charles de Gaulle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Airport" title="Istanbul Airport">Istanbul</a>.\nIn 2010, 65.9% of passengers using the airport flew to and from Europe, 11.7% to and from North America and 8.8% to and from Asia; cargo volume was mainly between Schiphol and Asia (45%) and North America (17%).<sup id="cite_ref-annual2010_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annual2010-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2010, 106 carriers provided a total of 301 destinations on a regular basis. Passenger destinations were offered by 91 airlines. Direct (non-stop) destinations grew by nine to a total of 274. Regular destinations serviced exclusively by full freighters (non-passenger) grew by eight to a total of twenty-seven.<sup id="cite_ref-Annual2009_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Annual2009-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airport is built as one large terminal (a single-terminal concept), split into three large departure halls, which connect again once airside. The most recent of these was completed in 1994 and expanded in 2007 with a new section, called Terminal&#160;4, although it is not considered a separate building. A new pier is to be opened in 2019 with a terminal extension planned to be operational by 2023. Plans for further terminal and gate expansion exist, including the construction of a separate new terminal between the Zwanenburgbaan and Polderbaan runways that would end the one-terminal concept.\n</p><p>Because of intense traffic and high landing fees (due to the limit of 500,000 flights a year), some <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost carriers</a> decided to move their flights to smaller airports, such as <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam_The_Hague_Airport" title="Rotterdam The Hague Airport">Rotterdam The Hague Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eindhoven_Airport" title="Eindhoven Airport">Eindhoven Airport</a>. Many low-cost carriers, such as <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>, however, continue to operate at Schiphol, using the low-cost H&#160;pier. <a href="/wiki/Lelystad_Airport" title="Lelystad Airport">Lelystad Airport</a> is currently being expanded aimed at accommodating some of the low-cost and leisure flights currently operating out of Schiphol, eventually taking up to 45,000 flights a year.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heer_kruisheer_zet_ford_2zitter_op_lier_chassis_schiphol_9_april_1933.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Heer_kruisheer_zet_ford_2zitter_op_lier_chassis_schiphol_9_april_1933.jpg/220px-Heer_kruisheer_zet_ford_2zitter_op_lier_chassis_schiphol_9_april_1933.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Heer_kruisheer_zet_ford_2zitter_op_lier_chassis_schiphol_9_april_1933.jpg/330px-Heer_kruisheer_zet_ford_2zitter_op_lier_chassis_schiphol_9_april_1933.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Heer_kruisheer_zet_ford_2zitter_op_lier_chassis_schiphol_9_april_1933.jpg/440px-Heer_kruisheer_zet_ford_2zitter_op_lier_chassis_schiphol_9_april_1933.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="314" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heer_kruisheer_zet_ford_2zitter_op_lier_chassis_schiphol_9_april_1933.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Ford being used to power a winch for towing gliders at Schiphol in 1933</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schiphol_verkeerstoren.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Schiphol_verkeerstoren.jpg/220px-Schiphol_verkeerstoren.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Schiphol_verkeerstoren.jpg/330px-Schiphol_verkeerstoren.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Schiphol_verkeerstoren.jpg/440px-Schiphol_verkeerstoren.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2496" data-file-height="1812" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schiphol_verkeerstoren.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The air traffic control tower at Schiphol in 1960</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Martinair_Convair_440.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Martinair_Convair_440.jpg/220px-Martinair_Convair_440.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Martinair_Convair_440.jpg/330px-Martinair_Convair_440.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Martinair_Convair_440.jpg/440px-Martinair_Convair_440.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Martinair_Convair_440.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Airplanes and service vehicles on the apron in 1965</div></div></div>\n<p>Before 1852, the entire <a href="/wiki/Polder" title="Polder">polder</a> of <a href="/wiki/Haarlemmermeer" title="Haarlemmermeer">Haarlemmermeer</a> in which the airport lies was a large lake with some shallow areas. There are multiple stories of how the place got its name. The most popular story is that in the shallow waters sudden violent storms could claim many ships. Winds were particularly strong in the Schiphol area since the prevailing wind direction is from the south-west, and Schiphol lies in the north-eastern corner of the lake. In English, <i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">schiphol</i> translates to \'ships hell\', a reference to many ships supposedly lost in the lake. When the lake was reclaimed, however, no shipwrecks were found. Another possible origin of the name is the word <i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">scheepshaal</i>. A <i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">scheepshaal</i> is a ditch<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> or small canal in which ships would be towed from one lake to another. A third explanation would be that the name derived from the words <i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">schip hol</i>. This is a low-lying area of land (<i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">hol</i>) from where wood would be obtained to build ships.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the lake was dredged in the mid-1800s, a fortification named Fort Schiphol was built in the area which was part of the <a href="/wiki/Stelling_van_Amsterdam" title="Stelling van Amsterdam">Stelling van Amsterdam</a> defence works.<sup id="cite_ref-stelling_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stelling-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Schiphol opened on 16 September 1916 as a military airbase, with a few barracks and a field serving as platform<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and runways. When civil aircraft started to use the field (17 December 1920), it was often called <i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">Schiphol-les-bains</i>. The <a href="/wiki/Fokker" title="Fokker">Fokker</a> aircraft manufacturer started a factory near Schiphol airport in 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The end of the First World War also saw the beginning of civilian use of Schiphol Airport and the airport eventually lost its military role completely.\n</p><p>By 1940, Schiphol had four asphalt runways at 45-degree angles, all 1,020 metres (3,350&#160;ft) or less. One was extended to become today\'s runway 04/22; two others crossed that runway at <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r994658806"/><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;params=52.312_N_4.8_E_type:landmark_region:NL"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">52\xc2\xb018\xe2\x80\xb243\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">4\xc2\xb048\xe2\x80\xb200\xe2\x80\xb3E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">52.312\xc2\xb0N 4.800\xc2\xb0E</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">52.312; 4.800</span></span></span></a></span>. The airport was captured by the German military that same year and renamed <i lang="de" title="German-language text">Fliegerhorst Schiphol</i>. A large number of anti-aircraft defences were installed in the vicinity of the airport and fake decoy airfields were constructed in the vicinity near <a href="/wiki/Bennebroek" title="Bennebroek">Bennebroek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vijfhuizen" title="Vijfhuizen">Vijfhuizen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vogelenzang" title="Vogelenzang">Vogelenzang</a> to try to confuse allied bombers. A railway connection was also built. Despite these defences, the airfield was still bombed intensively; an exceptionally heavy attack on 13 December 1943 caused so much damage that it rendered the airfield unusable as an active base. After that, it served only as an emergency landing field, until the Germans themselves destroyed the remnants of the airfield at the start of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Market_Garden" title="Operation Market Garden">Operation Market Garden</a>. At the end of the war, the airfield was quickly restored: the first aircraft, a <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">Douglas DC-3</a>, landed on 8 July 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A new terminal building was completed in 1949 and it was decided that Schiphol was to become the primary airport of the Netherlands. The expansion came at the cost of a small town called Rijk, which was demolished to make room for the growing airport. The name of this town is remembered in the name of the present <a href="/wiki/Schiphol-Rijk" title="Schiphol-Rijk">Schiphol-Rijk</a> industrial estate. In 1967, Schiphol expanded even further with a new terminal area at its current location. Most of the 1967 terminal is still in use today (Departure Halls 1 and 2) as are parts of the original piers (now called C, D, and E). Dutch designer Benno Wissing created signage for Schiphol Airport, well known for its clear writing and thorough colour-coding; to avoid confusion, he prohibited any other signage in the shades of yellow and green used.<sup id="cite_ref-rawthorn_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rawthorn-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The new terminal building replaced the older facilities once located on what is now the east side of the airport. The A-Pier (now C-pier) of the airport was modified in 1970 to allow <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a> aircraft to use the boarding gates. A new pier (D, now called F) opened in 1977, dedicated to handling wide-body aircraft. The first railway station at the airport followed in 1978.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_since_the_1990s">Development since the 1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Development since the 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schiphol-overview.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Schiphol-overview.png/220px-Schiphol-overview.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Schiphol-overview.png/330px-Schiphol-overview.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Schiphol-overview.png/440px-Schiphol-overview.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schiphol-overview.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing the six runways of Schiphol</div></div></div>\n<p>The construction of a new Air Traffic Control tower was completed in 1991 as the existing tower could no longer oversee all of the airports as it was further expanded. Departure Hall 3 was added to the terminal in 1993, as was another pier, G-pier. New wayfinding signage was designed that year as well by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Mijksenaar" title="Paul Mijksenaar">Paul Mijksenaar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> A sixth runway was completed at quite some distance west of the rest of airport in 2003 and was nicknamed the Polderbaan, with the connecting <a href="/wiki/Taxiway_bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Taxiway bridge">taxiway crossing</a> the <a href="/wiki/A5_motorway_(Netherlands)" title="A5 motorway (Netherlands)">A5 motorway</a>. The distance of this runway means that taxi times to and from this runway can take between 10 and 20 minutes. It also required the construction of an additional Air Traffic Control tower as the primary tower is too far away to oversee this part of the airfield.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><span class="anchor" id="Diamond_heist"></span>On 25 February 2005, a diamond robbery occurred at Schiphol\'s cargo terminal. The robbers used a stolen KLM van to gain <a href="/wiki/Airside_(airport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Airside (airport)">airside</a> access. The estimated value of the stones was around 75 million <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euros</a>, making it one of the largest diamond robberies ever.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Later in 2005, a fire broke out at the airport\'s detention centre, killing 11 people and injuring 15. The complex was holding 350 people at the time of the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_Schiphol_2005_fire_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Schiphol_2005_fire-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\nResults from the investigation almost one year later showed that fire safety precautions were not in force. A national outrage resulted in the resignation of Justice Minister <a href="/wiki/Piet_Hein_Donner" title="Piet Hein Donner">Piet Hein Donner</a> (CDA) and Mayor Hartog of Haarlemmermeer. Spatial Planning Minister <a href="/wiki/Sybilla_Dekker" title="Sybilla Dekker">Sybilla Dekker</a> (VVD) resigned as well, because she bore responsibility for safety failings cited in the report.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal">Terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Schiphol_Airport_entry.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Amsterdam_Schiphol_Airport_entry.jpg/220px-Amsterdam_Schiphol_Airport_entry.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Amsterdam_Schiphol_Airport_entry.jpg/330px-Amsterdam_Schiphol_Airport_entry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Amsterdam_Schiphol_Airport_entry.jpg/440px-Amsterdam_Schiphol_Airport_entry.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4066" data-file-height="2765" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Schiphol_Airport_entry.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main entry of Amsterdam Airport Schiphol.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Europa_2015_(1084).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Europa_2015_%281084%29.jpg/220px-Europa_2015_%281084%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Europa_2015_%281084%29.jpg/330px-Europa_2015_%281084%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Europa_2015_%281084%29.jpg/440px-Europa_2015_%281084%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Europa_2015_(1084).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Check-in hall interior at the Amsterdam Airport Schiphol.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luchthaven_Schiphol_Amsterdam_Airport_KLM_Cargo_Boeing_Jumbo_Taxiway_Bridge_Highway_A4_E19_Foto_Wolfgang_Pehlemann_IMG_2267.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Luchthaven_Schiphol_Amsterdam_Airport_KLM_Cargo_Boeing_Jumbo_Taxiway_Bridge_Highway_A4_E19_Foto_Wolfgang_Pehlemann_IMG_2267.jpg/220px-Luchthaven_Schiphol_Amsterdam_Airport_KLM_Cargo_Boeing_Jumbo_Taxiway_Bridge_Highway_A4_E19_Foto_Wolfgang_Pehlemann_IMG_2267.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Luchthaven_Schiphol_Amsterdam_Airport_KLM_Cargo_Boeing_Jumbo_Taxiway_Bridge_Highway_A4_E19_Foto_Wolfgang_Pehlemann_IMG_2267.jpg/330px-Luchthaven_Schiphol_Amsterdam_Airport_KLM_Cargo_Boeing_Jumbo_Taxiway_Bridge_Highway_A4_E19_Foto_Wolfgang_Pehlemann_IMG_2267.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Luchthaven_Schiphol_Amsterdam_Airport_KLM_Cargo_Boeing_Jumbo_Taxiway_Bridge_Highway_A4_E19_Foto_Wolfgang_Pehlemann_IMG_2267.jpg/440px-Luchthaven_Schiphol_Amsterdam_Airport_KLM_Cargo_Boeing_Jumbo_Taxiway_Bridge_Highway_A4_E19_Foto_Wolfgang_Pehlemann_IMG_2267.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luchthaven_Schiphol_Amsterdam_Airport_KLM_Cargo_Boeing_Jumbo_Taxiway_Bridge_Highway_A4_E19_Foto_Wolfgang_Pehlemann_IMG_2267.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/KLM_Cargo" class="mw-redirect" title="KLM Cargo">KLM Cargo</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400ERF" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 747-400ERF">Boeing 747-400ERF</a> on the Taxiway Bridge crossing the Highway A4 E19.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schiphol_Tower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Schiphol_Tower.jpg/220px-Schiphol_Tower.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Schiphol_Tower.jpg/330px-Schiphol_Tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Schiphol_Tower.jpg/440px-Schiphol_Tower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4609" data-file-height="3073" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schiphol_Tower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Schiphol Tower</div></div></div>\n<p>Schiphol uses a one-terminal concept, where all facilities are located under a single roof, radiating from the central plaza, Schiphol Plaza. The terminal is divided into three sections or halls designated 1, 2 and 3. The piers and concourses of each hall are connected so that it is possible, on both sides of security or border inspection, to walk between piers and halls, although border control separates <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen</a> from non-Schengen areas. The exception to this is the low-cost pier M: once airside (past security), passengers cannot access any other areas.\n</p><p>Schiphol Airport has approximately 223 <sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> boarding gates including eighteen double <a href="/wiki/Jetway" class="mw-redirect" title="Jetway">jetway</a> gates used for widebody aircraft. The airport adopted a distinctive design, with the second jetway extending over the aircraft wing hanging from a steel cantilever structure. Recent refurbishments have seen most of these jetways being replaced with a more conventional layout. Two gates feature a third jetway for handling of the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>. <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> was the first airline to fly the A380 to Schiphol in August 2012, deploying the aircraft on its double daily Dubai\xe2\x80\x93Amsterdam service.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> During the summer, <a href="/wiki/China_Southern_Airlines" title="China Southern Airlines">China Southern Airlines</a> also uses the A380 on its Beijing\xe2\x80\x93Amsterdam route.\n</p><p>Schiphol has large <a href="/wiki/Shopping_mall" title="Shopping mall">shopping areas</a> as a source of revenue and as an additional attraction for passengers. Schiphol Plaza not only connects the three halls but also houses a large shopping centre and the railway station, also attracting general visitors.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Departure_Hall_1">Departure Hall 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Departure Hall 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Departure Hall 1 consists of Piers B and C, both of which are dedicated Schengen areas and shares D-pier with Departure hall 2. Pier B has 14 gates and Pier C has 21 gates.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Departure_Hall_2">Departure Hall 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Departure Hall 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Departure Hall 2 consists of Piers D and E.\n</p><p>Pier D is the largest pier and has two levels. The lower floor houses non-Schengen flights and the upper floor is used for Schengen flights. By using stairs, the same jetways are used to access the aircraft. Schengen gates are numbered beginning with D-59; non-Schengen gates are numbered from D-1 to D-57.\n</p><p>Pier E is a dedicated non-Schengen area and has 14 gates. It is typically home to <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> hub airlines <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a> and <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a>, along with other members, such as <a href="/wiki/China_Airlines" title="China Airlines">China Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/China_Southern_Airlines" title="China Southern Airlines">China Southern Airlines</a>. Other Middle Eastern and Asian airlines such as <a href="/wiki/Air_Astana" title="Air Astana">Air Astana</a>, <a href="/wiki/EVA_Air" title="EVA Air">EVA Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iran_Air" title="Iran Air">Iran Air</a> also typically operate out of Pier E.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Departure_Hall_3">Departure Hall 3</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Departure Hall 3">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Departure Hall 3 consists of three piers: F, G, and H/M. Pier F has 8 gates and is typically dominated by SkyTeam members such as primary airline KLM, <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Airways" title="Kenya Airways">Kenya Airways</a>, China Airlines and China Southern Airlines, and other members. Pier G has 13 gates. Piers F and G are non-Schengen areas.\n</p><p>Piers H and M are physically one concourse consisting of 7 shared gates and are home to <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost airlines</a>. Operating completely separately, H handles non-Schengen flights while M is dedicated to flights within the Schengen area.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="A380">A380</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: A380">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Gates G9, E18 and E22 (E22 refurbished in 2019) are equipped to handle daily <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> service by <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> and <a href="/wiki/China_Southern_Airlines" title="China Southern Airlines">China Southern Airlines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="General_aviation_terminal">General aviation terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: General aviation terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>A new <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a> terminal was opened in 2011 on the east side of the airport, operated as the <i>KLM Jet Center</i>. The new terminal building has a floorspace of 6,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (65,000&#160;sq&#160;ft); 1,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (11,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) for the actual terminal and lounges, 4,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (43,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) for office space and 1,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (11,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) for parking.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_facilities">Other facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Other facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam" class="mw-redirect" title="Rijksmuseum Amsterdam">Rijksmuseum</a> operates an annex at the airport, offering a small overview of both classical and contemporary art.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Admission to the exhibits is free.\n</p><p>In summer 2010, Schiphol Airport Library opened alongside the museum, providing passengers access to a collection of 1,200 books (translated into 29 languages) by Dutch authors on subjects relating to the country\'s history and culture. The 89.9&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (968&#160;sq&#160;ft) library offers e-books and music by Dutch artists and composers that can be downloaded free of charge to a laptop or mobile device.<sup id="cite_ref-clark_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clark-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For aviation enthusiasts, Amsterdam Airport Schiphol has a large rooftop viewing area, called the Panoramaterras. It is not accessible to connecting passengers unless they first exit the airport. Enthusiasts and the public can enter, free of charge, from the airport\'s landside. Since June 2011, it is the location for a <a href="/wiki/KLM_Cityhopper" title="KLM Cityhopper">KLM Cityhopper</a> <a href="/wiki/Fokker_100" title="Fokker 100">Fokker 100</a>, modified to be a viewing exhibit.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Besides the Panoramaterras, Schiphol has other spotting sites, especially along the newest Polderbaan runway and at the <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald&#39;s">McDonald\'s</a> restaurant at the north side of the airport.\n</p><p>Schiphol has its own <a href="/wiki/Mortuary" class="mw-redirect" title="Mortuary">mortuary</a>, where the dead can be handled and kept before departure or after arrival. Since October 2006, people can also hold a wedding ceremony at Schiphol.<sup id="cite_ref-baskas_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baskas-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Schiphol also has a new state-of-the-art cube-shaped Hilton Amsterdam Airport Schiphol with 433 rooms, rounded corners and diamond-shaped windows. The spacious <a href="/wiki/Atrium_(architecture)" title="Atrium (architecture)">atrium</a> has a 41-metre-high (135&#160;ft) ceiling made of glass and is in the heart of the building. A covered walkway connects the hotel directly to the terminal. The hotel was completed in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_expansions">Future expansions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Future expansions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Schiphol_Group" title="Schiphol Group">Schiphol Group</a> announced an expansion of Schiphol, featuring a new pier,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> an expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">terminal</a>, and a new parking garage.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Pier A will be part of Departure Hall 1, which already has Pier B (14 gates) and Pier C (21 gates). The new Pier A will have 5 <a href="/wiki/Narrow-body_aircraft" title="Narrow-body aircraft">narrow-body</a> gates and will initially have 3 <a href="/wiki/Wide-body_aircraft" title="Wide-body aircraft">wide-body</a> gates, with two more planned for a later phase.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The first activities are expected to start in 2017 and to be completed in 2023. The expansions will cost about 500 million <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euros</a>.\n</p><p>First, the new Pier A will be built to the southwest of Pier B, in an area currently used as a freight platform. Expected to be operational by the end of 2019, pier A will mainly be used for flights within <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. To handle future growth in passengers, Schiphol will further expand the <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">terminal</a> and build a fourth departure hall with facilities for both departures and arrivals. From this new building, direct access will be made to Schiphol Plaza, continuing the one-terminal concept. When finished in 2023, Schiphol will be able to handle over 70 million passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Due to rapid growth of Schengen passengers during 2016, Schiphol was however forced to rapidly build a temporary departure hall which opened in March 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Schiphol\'s growth is hampered by slot restrictions from the government. For reasons of safety and noise reduction, Schiphol is allowed to have no more than 500,000 aircraft movements until the end of 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> A proposal to increase the limit to 540,000 movements from 2021 onwards has been postponed until a new government is formed after the elections in March 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> As Schiphol nearly approached the limit of 500,000 in the last few years, the slot restrictions have hindered airlines to settle at Schiphol. Among airlines that have expressed interest in flying at Schiphol are <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Airways" title="Atlantic Airways">Atlantic Airways</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Somon_Air" title="Somon Air">Somon Air</a><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/WestJet" title="WestJet">WestJet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tower">Tower</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tower">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Schiphol <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_control" title="Air traffic control">air traffic control</a> tower, with a height of 101&#160;m (331&#160;ft), was the tallest in the world when constructed in 1991. Schiphol is geographically one of the world\'s lowest major commercial airports. The entire airport is below sea level. The lowest point sits at 3.4&#160;m (11&#160;ft) below sea level: 1.4&#160;m (4.5&#160;ft) below the Dutch <a href="/wiki/Normaal_Amsterdams_Peil" class="mw-redirect" title="Normaal Amsterdams Peil">Normaal Amsterdams Peil</a> (NAP). The runways are around 3&#160;m (9.8&#160;ft) below NAP.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Runways">Runways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Runways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Schiphol has six <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runways</a>, one of which is used mainly by <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AIP_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> AMS covers a total area of 6,887 acres (2,787 ha) of land.<sup id="cite_ref-landArea_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-landArea-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="width:99%;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Number\n</th>\n<th>Runway direction/code\n</th>\n<th>Length<br /> <span class="nowrap">(in metres</span> <span class="nowrap">and feet)</span>\n</th>\n<th>Width<br /> <span class="nowrap">(in metres</span> <span class="nowrap">and feet)</span>\n</th>\n<th>Common name\n</th>\n<th>Source of the name\n</th>\n<th>Surface\n</th>\n<th>Notes\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1</td>\n<td>18R/36L</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">3,800&#160;m<br />12,467&#160;ft</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">60&#160;m<br />197&#160;ft</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><b>Polderbaan</b></td>\n<td>Decided via contest. <a href="/wiki/Polder" title="Polder">Polder</a> is the Dutch word for land reclaimed from a body of water. Schiphol Airport is situated in a polder.</td>\n<td>Asphalt</td>\n<td>Newest runway, opened in 2003. Own control tower.<br />Located to reduce the noise impact on the surrounding population. class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Other users">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Other regular users of Schiphol are the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Coastguard" title="Netherlands Coastguard">Netherlands Coastguard</a> whose aircraft are operated by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Air_Force" title="Royal Netherlands Air Force">Royal Netherlands Air Force</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dienst_Luchtvaart_Politie" Association</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />68.1\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_facilities_2">Other facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Other facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schiphol_Group_offices.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Schiphol_Group_offices.JPG/220px-Schiphol_Group_offices.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Schiphol_Group_offices.JPG/330px-Schiphol_Group_offices.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Schiphol_Group_offices.JPG/440px-Schiphol_Group_offices.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schiphol_Group_offices.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Schiphol_Group" title="Schiphol Group">Schiphol Group</a> offices</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_Cityhopper_offices_Schiphol-Oost.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/KLM_Cityhopper_offices_Schiphol-Oost.jpg/220px-KLM_Cityhopper_offices_Schiphol-Oost.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/KLM_Cityhopper_offices_Schiphol-Oost.jpg/330px-KLM_Cityhopper_offices_Schiphol-Oost.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/KLM_Cityhopper_offices_Schiphol-Oost.jpg/440px-KLM_Cityhopper_offices_Schiphol-Oost.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_Cityhopper_offices_Schiphol-Oost.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Convair Building, which houses <a href="/wiki/KLM_Cityhopper" title="KLM Cityhopper">KLM Cityhopper</a> and KLM offices, and the original Schiphol control tower</div></div></div>\n<p>The TransPort Building on the Schiphol Airport property houses the head offices of <a href="/wiki/Martinair" title="Martinair">Martinair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transavia.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Transavia.com">Transavia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Newbuild_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newbuild-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Construction of the building, which has 10,800&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (116,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) of rentable space, began on 17 March 2009. <a href="/wiki/Schiphol_Group" title="Schiphol Group">Schiphol Group</a> and the architect firm Paul de Ruiter designed the building, while De Vries and Verburg, a firm of <a href="/wiki/Stolwijk" title="Stolwijk">Stolwijk</a>, constructed the building.<sup id="cite_ref-martinairNew_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-martinairNew-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The World Trade Center Schiphol Airport houses the head office of <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-milestone_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-milestone-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wtc_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wtc-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> the Netherlands office of <a href="/wiki/China_Southern_Airlines" title="China Southern Airlines">China Southern Airlines</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-chinas_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chinas-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> and the Netherlands offices of <a href="/wiki/Iran_Air" title="Iran Air">Iran Air</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> The head office of <a href="/wiki/Schiphol_Group" title="Schiphol Group">Schiphol Group</a>, the airport\'s operator, is located on the airport property.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> The Convair Building, with its development beginning after a parcel was earmarked for its development in 1999, houses KLM offices,<sup id="cite_ref-Annual1999Page35_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Annual1999Page35-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> including KLM Recruitment Services and the head office of <a href="/wiki/KLM_Cityhopper" title="KLM Cityhopper">KLM Cityhopper</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Recruit_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Recruit-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The original control tower of Schiphol Airport, which the airport authorities had moved slightly from its original location, now houses a restaurant.<sup id="cite_ref-Annual1999Page35_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Annual1999Page35-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The area <a href="/wiki/Schiphol-Rijk" title="Schiphol-Rijk">Schiphol-Rijk</a> includes the head offices of <a href="/wiki/TUI_fly_Netherlands" title="TUI fly Netherlands">TUI fly Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airlines" title="Amsterdam Airlines">Amsterdam Airlines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At one time, <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a> had its head office briefly on the grounds of Schiphol Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Its current head office in nearby <a href="/wiki/Amstelveen" title="Amstelveen">Amstelveen</a> had a scheduled completion at the end of 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Previously Martinair had its head office in the Schiphol Center (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Schiphol Centrum</i>) at Schiphol Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-Martinhist_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martinhist-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Formerly, the head office of Transavia was in the Building Triport III at Schiphol Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/NLM_Cityhopper" class="mw-redirect" title="NLM Cityhopper">NLM Cityhopper</a> and later KLM Cityhopper previously had their head offices in Schiphol Airport building 70.<sup id="cite_ref-flightglobal.com_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flightglobal.com-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nippon_Cargo_Airlines" title="Nippon Cargo Airlines">Nippon Cargo Airlines</a> has its Europe regional headquarters at Schiphol.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> The National Aerospace Museum Aviodome\xe2\x80\x93Schiphol was previously located at Schiphol.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, the museum moved to <a href="/wiki/Lelystad_Airport" title="Lelystad Airport">Lelystad Airport</a> and was renamed the "<a href="/wiki/Aviodrome" title="Aviodrome">Aviodrome</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transport">Ground transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Ground transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schipholspoortunnel1992.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Schipholspoortunnel1992.jpeg/220px-Schipholspoortunnel1992.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Schipholspoortunnel1992.jpeg/330px-Schipholspoortunnel1992.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Schipholspoortunnel1992.jpeg/440px-Schipholspoortunnel1992.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="715" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schipholspoortunnel1992.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The construction of the tunnel and railway station in 1992</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Schiphol_Airport_railway_station" title="Schiphol Airport railway station">Schiphol Airport railway station</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Nederlandse_Spoorwegen" title="Nederlandse Spoorwegen">Nederlandse Spoorwegen</a> (NS), the national Dutch train operator, has a major passenger railway station directly underneath the passenger terminal complex that offers transportation 24 hours a day into the four major cities Amsterdam, <a href="/wiki/Utrecht_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Utrecht (city)">Utrecht</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>. There are efficient and often direct services to many other cities in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> There are intercity connections to <a href="/wiki/Almere" title="Almere">Almere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lelystad" title="Lelystad">Lelystad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Centraal_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Centraal railway station">Amsterdam Centraal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utrecht_Centraal_railway_station" title="Utrecht Centraal railway station">Utrecht Centraal</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Den_Haag_Centraal_railway_station" title="Den Haag Centraal railway station">The Hague Centraal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Den_Haag_Hollands_Spoor_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Den Haag Hollands Spoor railway station">The Hague HS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam_Centraal_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Rotterdam Centraal railway station">Rotterdam Centraal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eindhoven_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Eindhoven railway station">Eindhoven</a>, <a href="/wiki/%27s-Hertogenbosch_railway_station" title="&#39;s-Hertogenbosch railway station">\'s-Hertogenbosch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeuwarden_railway_station" title="Leeuwarden railway station">Leeuwarden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Groningen_railway_station" title="Groningen railway station">Groningen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amersfoort_Centraal_railway_station" title="Amersfoort Centraal railway station">Amersfoort Centraal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apeldoorn_railway_station" title="Apeldoorn railway station">Apeldoorn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deventer_railway_station" title="Deventer railway station">Deventer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enschede_railway_station" title="Enschede railway station">Enschede</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arnhem_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Arnhem railway station">Arnhem Centraal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nijmegen_railway_station" title="Nijmegen railway station">Nijmegen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venlo_railway_station" title="Venlo railway station">Venlo</a>. Schiphol is also a stop for the <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">Thalys</a> international high-speed train, connecting the airport directly to <a href="/wiki/Antwerpen-Centraal_railway_station" title="Antwerpen-Centraal railway station">Antwerp</a>, Brussels and <a href="/wiki/Gare_du_Nord" title="Gare du Nord">Paris Gare du Nord</a>, as well as to <a href="/wiki/Bourg-Saint-Maurice" title="Bourg-Saint-Maurice">Bourg St Maurice</a> (winter) and <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a> (summer). The Intercity-Brussel (also named "beneluxtrein") to <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> stops at the airport.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Amsterdam Airport Schiphol is also easily accessible by bus, as many services call or terminate at the bus station located outside in front of the terminal building.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable vatop">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Destination\n</th>\n<th>Service(s)\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Aalsmeer" Express</i>"\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Amsterdam, <a href="/wiki/Osdorp" title="Osdorp">Osdorp</a>\n</td>\n<td>69, 194, 195, night bus N95\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Amsterdam, <a title="Leimuiden">Leimuiden</a>\n</td>\n<td>370\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Nieuw-Vennep" title="Nieuw-Vennep">Nieuw-Vennep</a>\n</td>\n<td>397, night bus N97\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a N30\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Zoetermeer" title="Zoetermeer">Zoetermeer</a>\n</td>\n<td>365\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The Taiwanese <a href="/wiki/EVA_Air" title="EVA Air">EVA Air</a> provides private bus services from Schiphol to Belgium for its Belgium-based customers. The service, which departs from and arrives at bus stop C11, goes to <a href="/wiki/Sint-Gillis" class="mw-redirect" title="Sint-Gillis">Sint-Gillis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> (near the <a href="/wiki/Brussels-South_railway_station" title="Brussels-South railway station">Brussels-South (Midi) railway station</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Berchem" title="Berchem">Berchem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> (near Antwerp-Berchem bus station). The service is co-operated with Reizen Lauwers NV.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Schiphol Airport can easily be reached by car via the <a href="/wiki/A4_motorway_(Netherlands)" title="A4 motorway (Netherlands)">A4</a> and <a href="/wiki/A9_motorway_(Netherlands)" title="A9 motorway (Netherlands)">A9</a> motorways.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While most roads leading to the airport are forbidden for bicycles, it is possible to reach the airport by bicycle via bicycle paths.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bijlmerramp2_without_link.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Bijlmerramp2_without_link.jpg/220px-Bijlmerramp2_without_link.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Bijlmerramp2_without_link.jpg/330px-Bijlmerramp2_without_link.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Bijlmerramp2_without_link.jpg/440px-Bijlmerramp2_without_link.jpg 2x" data-file-width="795" data-file-height="410" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bijlmerramp2_without_link.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The crash site of <a href="/wiki/El_Al_Flight_1862" title="El Al Flight 1862">El Al Flight 1862</a> in 1992</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Crash_Turkish_Airlines_TK_1951_complete_site.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Crash_Turkish_Airlines_TK_1951_complete_site.jpg/220px-Crash_Turkish_Airlines_TK_1951_complete_site.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Crash_Turkish_Airlines_TK_1951_complete_site.jpg/330px-Crash_Turkish_Airlines_TK_1951_complete_site.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Crash_Turkish_Airlines_TK_1951_complete_site.jpg/440px-Crash_Turkish_Airlines_TK_1951_complete_site.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1064" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Crash_Turkish_Airlines_TK_1951_complete_site.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The crash site of <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines_Flight_1951" title="Turkish Airlines Flight 1951">Turkish Airlines Flight 1951</a> on 25 February 2009</div></div></div>\n<ul><li>On 14 November 1946, a <a href="/wiki/C-47_Skytrain" class="mw-redirect" title="C-47 Skytrain">Douglas C-47</a> operated by KLM from London approached Schiphol during bad weather conditions. The first two attempts to land failed. During the third attempt, the pilot realized that the airplane was not lined up properly with the runway. The aircraft made a sharp left turn at low speed, causing the left wing to hit the ground. The airplane crashed and caught fire, killing all 26 people on board.</li>\n<li>On 4 October 1992, <a href="/wiki/El_Al_Flight_1862" title="El Al Flight 1862">El Al Flight 1862</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 747-200">Boeing 747-200</a>F cargo jet en route to <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a>, lost both right-wing engines (#3 and #4) just after taking off from Schiphol and crashed into an apartment building in the <a href="/wiki/Bijlmer" class="mw-redirect" title="Bijlmer">Bijlmer</a> neighbourhood of Amsterdam while attempting to return to the airport. A total of 43 people were killed, including the plane\'s crew of three and a non-revenue passenger. In addition to these fatalities, 11 persons were seriously injured and 15 persons received minor injuries.</li>\n<li>On 4 April 1994, <a href="/wiki/KLM_Cityhopper_Flight_433" title="KLM Cityhopper Flight 433">KLM Cityhopper Flight 433</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Saab_340" title="Saab 340">Saab 340</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>, returned to Schiphol after setting the number two engine to flight idle because the crew mistakenly believed that the engine suffered from low oil pressure because of a faulty warning light. On final approach at a height of 90&#160;ft (27&#160;m), the captain decided to <a href="/wiki/Go-around" title="Go-around">go-around</a> and gave full throttle on only the number one engine, leaving the other in flight idle. The airplane rolled to the right, pitched up, stalled and hit the ground at 80 degrees bank. Of the twenty-four people on board, three were killed, including the captain. Nine others were seriously injured.</li>\n<li>On 25 February 2009, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines_Flight_1951" title="Turkish Airlines Flight 1951">Turkish Airlines Flight 1951</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-800">Boeing 737-800</a> from Istanbul crashed on approach, just 1&#160;km (0.6&#160;mi) short of the airport\'s Polderbaan runway. The plane carried 128 passengers and 7 crew on board. 9 people were killed and a further 86 were injured, including six with serious injuries. Four of the dead were employees of <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a>, involved in an advanced radar deal with Turkey. An initial report from the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Safety_Board" title="Dutch Safety Board">Dutch Safety Board</a> revealed that the left <a href="/wiki/Radio_altimeter" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio altimeter">radio altimeter</a> had failed to provide the correct height above the ground and suddenly reported \xe2\x88\x928&#160;ft (\xe2\x88\x922.4&#160;m). As a result of this the <a href="/wiki/Autothrottle" title="Autothrottle">autothrottle</a> system closed the thrust levers to idle, as it is programmed to reduce thrust when below 27&#160;ft (8.2&#160;m) radio altitude. This eventually resulted in a dropping airspeed that was not acted upon until it was too late to recover, and the aircraft <a href="/wiki/Stall_(flight)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stall (flight)">stalled</a> and crashed in a field.</li>\n<li>On 23 February 2017, a <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Canada_Dash_8#Series_400" title="De Havilland Canada Dash 8">Bombardier Dash-8 Q400</a> operated by <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a> suffered a <a href="/wiki/Dash_8_landing_gear_incidents" class="mw-redirect" title="Dash 8 landing gear incidents">collapse</a> of its right landing gear after landing at the Oostbaan.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> The plane took off from <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Airport" title="Edinburgh Airport">Edinburgh</a> after a 1.5-hour delay and had to battle <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_UK_and_Ireland_windstorm_season#Storm_Doris" title="2016\xe2\x80\x9317 UK and Ireland windstorm season">storm Doris</a> throughout the flight and during landing. None of the 59 passengers and 4 crew was injured in the incident, but the aircraft sustained significant damage.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_Netherlands" title="Transport in the Netherlands">Transport in the Netherlands</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hello_Goodbye_(TV_series)" title="Hello Goodbye (TV series)"><i>Hello Goodbye</i> (TV series)</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_passenger_air_routes" title="List of busiest passenger air routes">List of busiest passenger air routes</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
